General Contributions to the Northeast Volunteer Army

The Thrifty Efforts of the Jin Yun Factory: The Shanghai Municipal Electrical and Silk Weaving Factory Industry Association members, specifically the entire staff of the Jin Yun Silk Weaving Factory on Zhaofeng Road, recognizing the Northeast Volunteer Army's brave fight against the enemy and their contribution to the Party and the nation, initiated a food and clothing reduction campaign led by the factory manager, Mr. Wang Shiqiang, to accumulate funds for donating to the Northeast Volunteer Army. Currently, they have raised 500 silver dollars, which have been handed over to the Shanghai Bank for transfer to the front lines, as a small contribution to the brave soldiers fighting the enemy.

The Double Tenth Festival Pay of the Da Hua Factory: Since Mr. Gao Songfu took over as manager of the Da Hua Match Factory, he has been working hard to reorganize it. In the past three years, the factory's output has gradually increased. The factory's employees, deeply ashamed of the national humiliation since the January 28th Incident, expressed this sentiment during the factory affairs meeting in September to all the workers. Everyone was indignant. On the Double Tenth Festival, all factories stopped work for rest, and wages were paid as usual. The factory's workers voluntarily worked as usual, with double wages, and donated the extra amount to the Northeast to fulfill the duty of a citizen. All staff members contributed one day's salary from the Double Tenth Festival as a donation, estimated to be over 100 yuan. The exact amount will be announced after it is confirmed on that day. There is no shortage of enthusiastic gentlemen in the domestic industrial sector, and they will surely rise to the occasion upon hearing the news.

Fujian Education Department Continues to Donate 1,000 Yuan: To donate to the Northeast Volunteer Army, the Fujian Education Department had previously donated 4,000 yuan in two installments to the Shanghai Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association. Yesterday, the department sent another 1,000 yuan, representing donations from the educational sector in Fujian Province.

National Music Society Performance to Raise Funds for Disaster Relief, Third Day

Yesterday was the last day of the National Music Research Society's performance to raise funds for disaster relief in the Northeast. The audience was still crowded. The performed dramas included "Regret at the End of the Ming Dynasty," "White Gate Tower," "Yan Yang Tower," and "Meeting of Heroes," etc., lasting until 2 a.m. The society's representatives expressed gratitude to the audience on behalf of the Northeast refugees. In total, over 2,000 tickets were sold over the three days. All expenses were borne by the initiators, so that the proceeds from the tickets could truly benefit the disaster victims.

North China Representatives of the Aviation Construction Association Depart from Shanghai This Morning

Since the Chinese Aviation Construction Association began soliciting members, letters requesting membership and inquiries about establishing branches have been received from various provinces every day. The association held a regular meeting at the Continental Arcade on Nanjing Road yesterday. For investigation purposes, the association has appointed its design director, Zhu Lin, to promote the association in the Pingjin area and to connect with the association's directors in Ping, Xiong Bing San and Zhu Zi Qiao to develop plans for association affairs. The association also appointed its executive director, Yan Zhifang, to contact leaders from all walks of life in important cities such as Qingdao, Jinan, and Taiyuan, in order to awaken the people of North China, who are on the front lines of the anti-Japanese resistance, to work together to build aviation, to strengthen national defense, and to relieve national suffering. It is reported that Mr. Zhu and Mr. Yan left Shanghai this morning to travel to various provinces in North China.

Representatives of Villagers Enclosed by Two Railways Petitioned the Railway Department in Beijing Yesterday

In order to build new station sites, the Two Railways Bureau has designated villagers' houses and farmlands along the routes as construction zones. Among them are villagers from Wangjiajing, Zhangjiazhai, and Zhuxiang in Pengpu District. The bureau only needs 700 mu of land, but the area designated for enclosure is as much as 4,000 mu. Therefore, they petitioned the Railway Bureau, requesting that the villages of Wangjiajing, etc., not be included in the railway area. However, repeated petitions to Director Chen Xinghan were ineffective. Last night, six representatives, Hou Xuanqing, Hou Baocheng, Zhang Lingen, Tan Zhongsheng, Tao Wenyuan, and Tao Ailang, elected by the three villages, took the 11 p.m. express train to Beijing to petition Railway Minister Gu Mengyu, requesting exemption from enclosure to alleviate the people's hardships.

Oath of Office for Executive and Supervisory Committee Members of the Municipal Party Headquarters and District Party Headquarters

The executive and supervisory committee members of the sixth session of the municipal party headquarters and the executive and supervisory committee members of the district party headquarters have been elected according to law. It is reported that the new executive and supervisory committee members will hold a joint swearing-in ceremony at 10 a.m. today in the auditorium on the third floor of the municipal party headquarters. Wu Tiecheng, a member sent by the Central Executive Committee, will supervise the oath of office for the municipal executive and supervisory committee members, while Yu Hongjun, a member of the municipal party headquarters, will be the supervisor for the oath of office for the executive and supervisory committee members of the various districts.

Mr. Wang Boqun's Talk After Arriving in Shanghai

Sichuan Province is Vast, Resourceful, and Its People are Hardworking and Enduring

The Most Important Plan at Present Should Be to Build Railways

Mr. Wang Boqun, former Minister of Communications, was ordered by the National Government to inspect the three provinces of Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou. He has now returned to Shanghai. A reporter visited him at his residence and first asked about the results of his observations in Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou. Mr. Wang said, "I was ordered to inspect the three provinces, and because of the convenience of the journey, I first entered Sichuan Province. I spent more than two months in Sichuan and learned about its complex situation. I must first return to Nanjing to report, so I have not yet gone to Yunnan and Guizhou. I have traveled to almost all the important cities in Sichuan Province, and I have talked with officials and representatives of various organizations. I feel that the land is vast and resourceful, and there is everything needed for daily life. The people are hardworking and enduring, surpassing the rest of the country. However, the inconvenient transportation makes it impossible to break away from the handicraft era, and goods are abandoned on the ground, which is a great pity. Therefore, the most important plan at present is to build railways, which is the mother of all development. The total number of soldiers in Sichuan is more than 400,000, and the annual cost is about 100 million yuan. There is a so-called defense zone system, in which one leader controls tens of thousands or hundreds of thousands of soldiers, occupying a place and confronting each other, which is an obstacle to all unified facilities, and there is always the possibility of causing internal strife. This time, I met with the leaders and urged them to unite sincerely, work hard to develop, improve internal affairs, cultivate strength, and jointly face the national crisis. The leaders all expressed their agreement, realizing that too many soldiers and too much military spending would overwhelm the people, not only would they not be able to serve the country, but they themselves would also feel great difficulty." The reporter also asked Mr. Wang whether he had heard anything about the opium smuggling case on the Yongnian steamboat, which he had just taken eastward. Mr. Wang said, "I heard that the Yongnian ship is the fastest, and there is no need to transfer along the way, so I took it. Because I had to meet with Chairman Jiang in Hankou, I planned to disembark in Hankou. I originally brought six attendants, but they were stranded in Chengdu due to illness, so only four people traveled with me. The luggage was very simple. The Yongnian ship sailed directly from Chongqing to Shanghai, with thousands of passengers. There was almost no space on the deck. Eight days after departure, I heard that there was a trend of smuggling opium. I then gathered my attendants and warned the public officials to be honest and law-abiding, and not to carry prohibited items privately, and ordered them to pay special attention to the servants and other people, and to place the luggage separately. Whenever customs officials came, they should be allowed to inspect first. We stayed in Wanxian that day and followed these instructions. On the 9th, we arrived in Yichang. When I saw the customs officials arriving, I told them again to be sure to check everything and not to be lenient. As a result, hundreds of taels of smuggled opium were found in the luggage of a female passenger in the official cabin. On the 11th, we arrived in Hankou. Old colleagues from the transportation department and Commander Ye of the garrison came to meet us on the ship or on the shore. I then led my attendants and luggage to disembark after inspection. Unexpectedly, after I disembarked, the ship was searched and opium and morphine were found, and Mrs. Shuang, who was on the same ship, was also suspected of serious crimes, which was completely unexpected. The next day, I met with Chairman Jiang and requested that the matter be thoroughly investigated and dealt with severely, and it will soon come to light."

From 9 a.m. to 10 a.m., association affairs were discussed, chaired by Dr. Liu Ruiheng, with Dr. Zhuo Bi Men and Dr. Yu Yun as recorders. The Pudong Telephone Problem Was Inquired About Yesterday

Statement by the Telephone Company Authorities

The Shanghai Telephone Company's submarine cable connecting Pudong was damaged, causing users' calls to be temporarily suspended, which is very inconvenient. According to the company's authorities yesterday, the Shanghai Telephone Company has always taken convenience to the public as its service tenet. The news reported that the company had no intention of signing a new contract, which is not entirely true. Because the Shanghai Telephone Company operates a public utility, when it obtained the franchise from the Municipal Council, the two parties signed a contract stating that any contract the company signs with any party must be approved by the Municipal Council to be official. However, since the provisional contract draft was jointly signed by the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities and the Shanghai Telephone Bureau last winter, the Municipal Council has not yet approved it. Therefore, the company cannot make any progress. As for the current urgent desire to repair the Pujiang cable, it is entirely for the convenience of users. The laying of this cable has been going on for a long time, and it is very important for communication. Once it is interrupted, the impact on users is significant. Now, the company cannot carry out repairs and cannot help users.

The Hua Wu Steamer Ran Aground in Zhenjiang

The Bow Was Deeply Embedded in the Riverbank

A Steamer Was Sent to the Rescue Yesterday Afternoon

The Hua Wu steamer of the Nanhua Company in Shanghai ran aground near Zhenjiang while transporting cargo from Nanjing to Shanghai. The front of the ship was completely grounded on the riverbank, and the situation was quite dangerous. The Shanghai office has sent a steamer to the rescue. The details of the incident are as follows:

Transporting Coal to Shanghai: The Nanhua Shipping Company is run by Liu Shisun. It originally had four seagoing vessels. In recent years, the Hua Ping and Hua Yang have been sold, leaving only the Hua Wu to operate. This time, the ship went to Pukou to transport 6,800 tons of coal from the Zhongxing Coal Mine to Shanghai. It left Nanjing on Monday of this week. That night, the ship arrived in Zhenjiang, and due to fog, it ran aground. The ship's hull was trapped on the riverbank.

The Truth of the Grounding: The Hua Wu steamer has a deadweight of 7,000 tons. This time, it was loaded with 6,800 tons of coal, which was already overweight. On Monday night, the ship arrived at the Jinshan Temple on the upper reaches of Zhenjiang, and the weather suddenly changed, with heavy fog, making navigation difficult. At this time, if the river pilot was not careful, he would have turned the Hua Wu steamer sideways and ran it aground on the shoal on the riverbank. At that time, because of the heavy load and the rapid forward movement, the front half of the Hua Wu was grounded on the riverbank, and the lower half was still in the river, similar to the situation of the Zhaoshang Tonghua ship aground at Huangsangkou.

Unable to Escape Danger: After the ship ran aground, the shipowners initially tried to reverse the ship, but the coal inside the ship was all heavy cargo, and it was deeply trapped in the sand. Repeated reversing failed to move it even a bit, and instead made the ship more dangerous. At this point, shipowner Yang Honglin knew that it would not be easy to pull it out for a while, so he put down a small sampan and landed, took a train to Shanghai in Zhenjiang, reported to the head office, and discussed rescue methods.

Sending a Ship to Rescue: Yesterday, shipowner Yang arrived in Shanghai, reported the details of the accident to Liu Shisun, and agreed to send a powerful tugboat from Shanghai to Zhenjiang to tow it. It was agreed to ask Jardine Matheson to dispatch a large tugboat and bring a group of workers, led by shipowner Yang Honglin, to the opposite bank of Jinshan Temple yesterday afternoon to tow it. Whether it can be towed out immediately is still unknown, but according to reports, the front of the ship has been deeply embedded in the sand and mud, and the situation is quite dangerous. Whether it is damaged or not needs to be verified after it is towed out.

Shanghai Municipal Defense Corps Restoration Plan

Requesting the Municipal Government to Supplement Four Items of Equipment

Requiring an Expenditure of More Than 1,330,000 Yuan

After the January 28th Incident, the business of various agencies in the city was severely damaged and suffered great losses. The municipal government had previously issued a notice to its subordinate units, ordering them to separately formulate restoration and reorganization plans. Luo Jingyou, chairman of the Management Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Defense Corps, after receiving the order, immediately convened the committee members to discuss day and night, and completed the drafting of the corps' restoration plan a few days ago. Chairman Luo also submitted the plan to the municipal government yesterday, along with various budget charts. The original submission is recorded below: Presenting the request for the Municipal Defense Corps, which has been affected by the war, to be thoroughly reorganized to meet the needs. A restoration plan is respectfully submitted, hoping that it will be reviewed and approved, and that funds will be allocated for purchase and supplementation. I humbly observe that since the city has been affected by the January 28th War, the Municipal Government has issued notices to various bureaus, ordering them to formulate restoration plans separately within their respective areas of responsibility, and submit them for review, along with budget estimates. The Defense Corps is also under its jurisdiction and should follow suit. I humbly observe that the city's defense corps originated from the previous merchants' corps. It has a long history. Since the Xinhai Revolution and the Guichou Revolution and the Qi-Lu War, Shanghai has always been the first to bear the brunt. The local area is often in trouble. During these critical times, the militia has always made every effort. Moreover, as in the Xinhai Revolution, Chen Gongying used the power of the merchants' corps and finally achieved the restoration. These are all the past traces of the local defense corps, and it is not just about maintaining the local area. This time, the Japanese invaded Shanghai and the four borders were in turmoil. The entire Defense Corps was mobilized, without regard to dawn or dusk. Those in the war zone were naturally present, and those not in the war zone also did their best for the rear defense. In the end, the local area was able to live in peace. This is the credit of the military and police, but it is also due to the assistance of the militia. However, the city's Defense Corps has undergone this incident, and there are things that must be urgently restored and reorganized. I would like to list them clearly. I have found that at the beginning of the establishment of the district corps, the expenses were entirely reliant on the voluntary donations of local enthusiastic people, and there were no fixed funds. Therefore, the clothing, firearms, and other equipment were all simple and lacking. Since the Municipal Government took over, donations have been stopped. Although the city treasury has provided meager subsidies, it still feels extremely exhausted and unable to supplement. This time, the corps in the war zone have suffered almost complete losses, and the other district corps have also been affected, and most of them are nominally extinct. Looking around at the city's situation, the past and present are very different. In the future, the local security, in addition to the security team and the police, the Defense Corps has an unshirkable responsibility. The responsibility is as heavy as that, and the military strength is so decayed. If it is still not supplemented, how can it be worthy of the burden and expectations? Moreover, recently Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Hankou strongly advocated promoting the people's armed forces, and encouraged them by improving their treatment and increasing their powers. It is clear that the importance of the militia has long been recognized by the government. Your honor loves and protects the local defense corps in every possible way. Now, I would like to list the necessary supplements to the equipment of the city's Defense Corps as follows: (1) Supplementing firearms: I have found that the original firearms of the district corps are less than half in number, and many of them are unusable. Now, it is planned to fully supplement the missing rifles in addition to the available weapons and ammunition in each district corps, so that each member has one gun, and each gun is equipped with 500 rounds of ammunition. It is also planned to follow the example of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps and add two portable machine guns to each team to strengthen its strength. (2) Supplementing civil engineering equipment: I have found that the Defense Corps is a people's armed force, and its military equipment does not necessarily have to be as good as the army's, but civil engineering equipment is an indispensable item for defense, and it cannot but have considerable preparations. Now, it is planned to set up one-third of each team to increase defensive power in times of emergency. (3) Supplementing vehicles and telescopes: I have found that the city area is vast. Except for the urban area, where transportation is relatively convenient, there are many obstacles in the rural areas. In the event of an accident, the equipment for communication, patrols, transportation, and reconnaissance is practically indispensable. Now, it is planned to supplement them selectively to make them more agile. (4) Supplementing clothing: I have found that the clothing of the district corps has not been entirely prepared, and has been incomplete and incomplete for many years. The losses this time have been particularly great. It is not enough to supplement them all to rectify the military appearance and provide services. As for kettles and lunch boxes, they are indispensable items in times of emergency, and it is planned to add them all together. For the above four items, the association has realistically estimated that a total of 1,337,156 yuan is required, which is a long-term solution. Shanghai is located in a strategic location, and is related to the views of China and foreign countries. Foreigners do not hesitate to spend huge sums of money to run the merchants' corps in the concession, and the completeness of their equipment is beyond our reach. In the future, the importance of the Municipal Defense Corps is as described above, and its strength should be vigorously supplemented so that it can fulfill its duties. I respectfully request that your honor consider transferring it to the Songhu District Police Rear Committee to allocate funds for purchase in order to strengthen its strength and secure the local area. Whether it is feasible, I have combined the books and tables and submitted a document requesting it. I respectfully request that you review and instruct its implementation, which is for the public convenience. I respectfully submit to Wu, Mayor of Shanghai, with five sheets of the restoration plan and one copy of the budget estimate.

Ninth National Anti-Drug Campaign Week of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association

Outline of Propaganda

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association will hold the ninth National Anti-Drug Campaign Week today, and has issued the following outline of propaganda. This year marks the ninth National Anti-Drug Campaign Week. The previous eight sessions, although also filled with the cries of poppy tears and blood, the most shocking is the one this week. (Omission) Now, on the occasion of the ninth National Anti-Drug Campaign Week, the association is considering the current situation and looking forward to the future, and is dazed and confused, as if suffering a heavy blow. It dares to offer its sincere heart and respectfully requests all sectors of society not to be disappointed in this intractable opium disaster and to stop ignoring it. It also hopes that the government authorities can suddenly realize the conspiracy of the powerful enemy and their past mistakes, and resolutely awaken, strictly implement the opium ban, and implement the following smoking ban plans: (1) Find alternative sources of tax revenue and do not use opium public sales as a measure to quench thirst with poison. (2) Issue a general order to the military and political authorities of all provinces prohibiting them from forcing farmers to grow opium. (3) The prohibition of opium should be based on the principle of pure prohibition. (4) Earmark fines for the prohibition of opium to fund the prohibition of opium and anti-drug work. (5) The government's prohibition of opium should cooperate with the people. (6) If you want to strictly prohibit opium, you must first punish illegal officials. (7) Conduct a major investigation of the opium disaster, with the people responsible. (8) Designate the four provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, and Henan as model areas for the prohibition of opium. (9) Strictly manage and control narcotics. (10) Pay attention to the selection of people responsible for handling opium prohibition agencies. (11) Hire international experts and adopt good practices from various countries. The above-mentioned measures require the implementation of the government, and must rely on the supervision of the people. All compatriots must work together with the association to unite and shout, otherwise, only the association will be left to bear its weight, how can it not be destroyed, and the breath of the anti-drug movement will probably be silent for a long time. I hope all sectors of society will think deeply and provide assistance.

Resolution of the Xiang Sheng Iron Factory Labor Dispute

Both Parties Signed Ten Conditions

It Was Decided to Start Work on October 3

The Social Bureau summoned both parties yesterday to mediate the labor dispute at the Xiang Sheng Iron Factory in Pudong. As a result, ten conditions were signed and the resolution was announced. The details are as follows:

Mediation Situation: The Social Bureau summoned both labor and management parties at 2 p.m. yesterday to mediate. The labor representatives were Zhang Linhua, Lu Lianqing, Yi Chang, and Xia Zhenru, and the management representatives were Bao Naimen and Hamilton, with Gong Honggeng as the translator. The Municipal Party Headquarters was represented by Li Weixiong. Wang Gang, a staff member of the Third Section of the Social Bureau, chaired the meeting. First, the chairman announced that the case had been held for a long time, and the workers' lives were quite panic-stricken. He hoped that both parties would make concessions to resolve the issue. Then, the labor and management parties reported the direct negotiation process. Finally, they discussed the issues of the factory's resumption of work and the dismissal of workers for a long time. Finally, ten conditions for resolution were drafted. Both parties expressed their agreement and signed on the spot, announcing the resolution.

Conditions for Resolution: The labor and management parties signed ten conditions for resolution as follows: (1) The factory will resume work on October 3. (2) Of the 124 workers who regularly receive work permits but do not work in the factory, 15 will be reinstated, and the remaining 109 will be dismissed. Whether the remaining 10 of the 109 dismissed workers can be reinstated will be negotiated by the union and the factory. (3) 26 workers who have been absent from work for a long time will be allowed to be dismissed. (4) The numbers of the workers reinstated and dismissed in the second and third articles can be found in the list prepared by the factory, which will be signed by representatives of the party and government agencies and stored in the Social Bureau. (5) The factory will subsidize the workers' losses with 1,200 yuan. (6) All the unskilled workers will be issued permits. If the work is light, they will be allowed to work in shifts. There must be at least 73 people working every day (including Sundays). (7) The factory will change the daily wages of unskilled workers from a uniform 67 cents to 1.20 yuan, 1.80 yuan, and 67.5 cents, depending on their working ability. (8) The daily wages of unskilled workers No. 1 and No. 2 will be set at 1.20 yuan, and the daily wage of unskilled workers No. 3 will be 1.50 yuan. (9) The treatment of unskilled workers working night shifts will be the same as that of lathe workers, etc. (10) In the future, if the factory finds that a worker is not working in the factory during roll call, it must notify the respective foremen and the union of the number of the absent worker after 12:00 a.m. and before 5:00 p.m. on the same day, and post it in a conspicuous place. This article was agreed upon and signed by the representatives of both parties, and the mediation is established as a labor contract between the parties in dispute.

The Dispute Over Shanghai South Public Buses Is Not Over

Two Female Workers Continue Their Hunger Strike

Workers' Union Organizes a Donation Team to Raise Funds

The shutdown dispute of the Shanghai South Public Bus Company has been mediated by the party and government many times, but it has not been resolved. The details are recorded below.

Continuing the Hunger Strike: Ms. Xu Lie'e and Ms. Hou Tingfen, two female ticket sellers, declared a hunger strike after entering the factory the day before, because they were concerned about the difficulty of making a living and the fact that the dispute would not be easily resolved in a short time. Afterwards, Fan Guoren, a representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, personally went to the factory to persuade them to eat, but the female workers were determined and continued their hunger strike.

Joining of Various Departments: All the workers in the company's various departments, including ticket sellers, ticket writers, ticket inspectors, drivers, water fillers, coppersmiths, blacksmiths, carpenters, electricians, car washers, and car arrangers, etc., totaling more than ten departments, together with the fourth branch station in West Shanghai, Hongqiao, and Caojiadu, etc., a total of more than 180 people. When the company announced the suspension of business last month, in addition to the more than 80 workers from the ticket selling, ticket writing, ticket inspection, driving, and water filling departments who unanimously negotiated with the company, the workers from the copper, iron, electric, and wood departments, etc., all took a wait-and-see attitude. Now, the workers from the copper department, etc., seeing that the company's dispute is unlikely to be resolved, especially yesterday, representatives from the various departments, Liu Xingsheng, Zhang Ayou, and Zhu Chengxiu, etc., led all the workers from the various departments to join in, taking a unified action.

Fundraising by District: After all the workers were suspended by the company, they had no work and no income was interrupted. Especially during the serious period of the dispute, they felt economically difficult. They organized a fundraising team to appeal to various unions for practical assistance. It is planned to divide into teams and depart to fundraise in six districts: South Shanghai, the French Concession, Zhabei, the Public Concession, Pudong, East Shanghai, and West Shanghai.

The Truth of the Ningbo Road Assassination Case

The Deceased Was a First-Class Thug

The Assailant Was a Fruit Vendor

The Dispute Arose from Robbery

The Corpse Was Examined Yesterday

It was reported in yesterday's news that around 8 PM the night before, a man in a white cloth short shirt stabbed another man to death on Ningbo Road, and the assailant was arrested on the spot. It is now known that the assailant was a Shaoxing native named Wang Jinting, 34 years old, who set up a fruit stall at the entrance of Deshun Lane on Tianjin Road. The deceased was a first-class thug from Ningbo named Yue Menhai, 25 years old. On that day, Yue tried to extort money from Wang but failed. He forcibly snatched forty cents in small silver coins and thirty copper coins to escape. At that moment, Wang was extremely angry and stabbed him to death in the alley between the New Guangda Theater and the China Hotel. Subsequently, the Laozha Police Station ordered detectives to transport the deceased's body to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road and took the assailant back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they reported to the First Special District Court, which appointed Prosecutor Zhang Yaoguang to go to the office with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi to examine the body, ascended to the official seat and listened to the West Deputy Chief of the police station reported the circumstances at the time. Afterwards, the deceased's relative, Hu Ashui, claimed to be 48 years old, working as a cook in Datong Lane on Baike Road, and stated that the deceased was his wife's younger brother, whose family members all currently live in their hometown. Therefore, he was there to collect the body on their behalf. After obtaining the statement, Mr. Zhang ruled that the deceased Yue Menhai, male, was indeed stabbed to death before his death. The body was collected by his relative, Hu Ashui, who signed a guarantee for its burial. The assailant Wang Jinting was escorted by the police station to the Criminal Division of the Special Court, where Presiding Judge Feng Shide interrogated the defendant and ordered him to be detained for further review at a later date.

Two Letters Beside a Headless Male Corpse

Significantly Related to the Case

On the 25th of this month, a headless male corpse was discovered on Lincoln Road in western Shanghai. After a detailed examination by officials from the District Court, the head has not yet been found. The Sixth District Police Station, considering the bizarre nature of this case, immediately ordered an investigation. It was also discovered that Gu Defa is the same person as Gu Laosi, residing at No. 48, Gujia Lane, Zhoujiaqiao. The police were immediately dispatched to arrest him, but Gu had already fled. His wife, Gu Zhou, was detained. After questioning yielded no clues, she was handed over to the District Court yesterday for investigation.

Xu Zhaofa, a 23-year-old man from Gaoyou, residing at No. 146, Jiangbian Pier, Gaochang Temple, had been working at the arsenal. Due to the arsenal being ordered to close down, Xu became unemployed. Since the Great War, there have been many unemployed people in Shanghai, causing Xu to be unable to find work, leading to financial difficulties. Resentful of his poverty, he hanged himself in his room the night before. It was not until his wife, Xu Wu, discovered and tried to rescue him that it was already too late. She cried loudly, which was heard by the Gaochang Temple Police Station in the Second District. They immediately ordered the local leader to report to the District Court for an examination. The deceased's wife also petitioned the court to waive the examination.

The Qitai Steamer Catches Fire at the Wharf

Four Sailors Injured

The Qitai steamer of the Shanghai Jiejiang Company, arriving in Shanghai from Yichang, had some damage to its engine and was taken out of service for repairs. The steamer was berthed at the Zhaoshangju Central Wharf and requested the New Factory to send technicians and workers to repair the machinery. Yesterday at 5:35 PM, the lubricating oil in the engine room of the Qitai steamer, which used diesel fuel, suddenly exploded due to cold air entering the engine, causing a fire to spread. The chief engineer, Shen Ruichang, 39 years old, from Ningbo, was burned, his entire body charred black, and his life was in danger. The third engineer, Chen Zongxing, 26 years old, from Ningbo, was burned all over his body. The lower-level worker, Fan Agou, 35 years old, from Ningbo, and Li Changlin, 28 years old, also from Ningbo, were all burned all over their bodies. After the incident, the injured were immediately sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, and the police were notified to extinguish the fire on the ship. The hull of the ship was not severely damaged, but the four injured are in critical condition, with concerns for their lives.

China Bank Inspection Report

55th Time

The 55th inspection report of the Shanghai China Bank Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee states that the committee members and entrusted accountants, in accordance with the committee's regulations, inspected the Shanghai China Bank's issuance and inter-bank redemption coupon reserve vault on September 25, 1932. The inspection was also joined by the Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance. The inspection results are listed on the left: the total amount of redemption coupons issued was 97,469,137 yuan, including 54,381,141 yuan issued by the bank, 18,516,172 yuan used by inter-banks, and 24,571,824 yuan used by various banks and stores. Except for the portion used by various banks and stores, which will be inspected separately according to the original method, this inspection covers the inter-bank portion as follows: the amount issued by the bank and used by inter-banks was 72,897,313 yuan. The amount of reserves for redemption coupons for the bank and inter-banks was 72,897,313 yuan, including 47,552,570.04 yuan in cash reserves and 25,344,742.60 yuan in guarantee reserves. The above two items, with the cash reserves accounting for 60% and the guarantee reserves accounting for 40%, were all checked and found to be accurate. In accordance with Article 5 of the regulations, this formal report is hereby made. September 25, 1932. Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance; Wang Yansong, Pei Yunqing, representatives of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce; Xu Xinliu, Wang Zhixin, representatives of the Shanghai Banking Association; Chuan Songnian, Li Jisheng, representatives of the Shanghai Money Industry Association; Yan Xijin, Zhou Jiefan, representatives of the coupon-receiving banks and stores; Ye Zhuotang, Xu Jikun, Zhou Zongliang, Li Zhilian, representatives of the directors and supervisors of the Bank of China; Accountant Wang Zikang.

American Sailor Creates Trouble While Drunk

Turned Over to the American Consulate for Investigation

Sailor Nichols (transliteration) from the American warship "U.S.S. Rochester" was heavily drunk at 1:30 AM yesterday. He hired sampan No. 1014, belonging to Wang Ashou, at the Yangjingbang Bund pier to take him to the American warship on the opposite bank. The American sailor jumped onto the sampan and drove Wang Ashou ashore, taking control of the boat and rowing it into the river. Wang Ashou immediately invited his son, Wang Yutang, to chase after him in another boat. Unexpectedly, the American sailor Nichols used an oar to strike Wang Ashou's right arm and Wang Yutang's left arm. The father and son were injured and cried out for help in extreme pain. Patrol officer Lü Zhongyu, who was on duty with the Water Patrol Team, heard the cries and went to rescue them. Because it was dark, Officer Lü shone a flashlight on the American sailor. The American sailor, feeling guilty, jumped into the river and tried to swim away. Officer Lü managed to pull him out of the water and took him to the team along with Wang Ashou and his son. After Captain Zhu interrogated them, he learned that the foreign sailor had caused trouble while drunk and assaulted the boatmen. He immediately sent them to the Third Section of the General Bureau for investigation. Yesterday, Assistant Qu Sunyi of the Third Section contacted the American Consulate by telephone. American Consul Smers visited the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau and requested that the sailor be handed over to him to be taken back to the consulate for investigation. Assistant Qu stated to the American Consul that two boatmen had been assaulted by the sailor and requested that he be severely punished to prevent similar incidents from happening again. The American Consul agreed to deal with the matter according to the law. However, the sailor had no clothes on his upper body and was naked, which was a matter of dignity. The American Consul asked where the sailor's clothes were. It was said that he did not know after being drunk. The American Consul borrowed a shirt from Assistant Qu and had the sailor wear it before taking him back to the consulate for investigation.

In late autumn, dysentery is becoming more prevalent, often due to the lingering effects of heat and dampness from this summer, often presenting as both red and white dysentery, causing severe pain. He Zuowang of Xingye Bank and Lu Yaolin of Jing'an Villa both suffered severely from this condition and were treated and cured by Physician Xie Liheng of Meifuli, Pike Road. It is said that the treatment of dysentery starts with clearing and unblocking, then soothing and harmonizing, and finally clearing and transforming, all of which are effective. However, if opium is taken for temporary relief from the pain of dysentery, the turbid pathogens will be retained by the force of the opium and cannot be discharged smoothly, which will inevitably prolong the illness and lead to danger. Therefore, he always advises those suffering from dysentery not to take opium.

To the Editor: I recently read a news item in your newspaper on the 29th of this month, in the "Local News" section, titled "Trial of the Taihe Street House Demolition Dispute." The news item stated that the defendant's witness, Fuluoyin, is Russian, and that on September 3rd at 4:00 PM, he came to collect items for the second time, which Yu Yabu reported to the General Inspectorate and the Yulin Road Police Station, and a Western policeman was dispatched to make him leave. Judge Wang then ordered the bailiff to escort Zhang Ruitang to the Younigan Real Estate Department to take evidence. All of these statements are inconsistent with the facts. Our office has investigated that Luo Yin (transliteration) is British, not Russian. The Taihe Lane houses required necessary repairs, so after obtaining a permit from the Municipal Council, Mr. Fu, accompanied by the police, proceeded with the repairs. As for the statement that Judge Wang ordered the bailiff to escort Zhang Ruitang to our office to obtain evidence, it is even more untrue (remainder omitted). Letter from Lawyer Heckmond of Younigan Law Office, September 30th. I recently read a news item in your newspaper on the 29th of this month, in the "Local News" section, stating that Li Jisheng of Beichuan Sha is a foreigner, which does not correspond with the facts. According to investigation, Li Jisheng was extremely frugal in his childhood and wore discarded clothes abandoned by foreigners, and his eyes were like those of foreigners, so the villagers called him a foreigner, not because a foreigner gave him jewelry that he had this title. His family has only a hundred acres of meager land, which is barely enough to make a living, and he cannot be called a wealthy man. What your newspaper said must be based on inaccurate rumors. Please correct this mistake. Sincerely, Li Fengming, September 30th.

Free Talk

One or Two Words

The Words of Negation in the Wu Dialect

— Zhanlu

When Suzhou people talk about an unsatisfactory person and negate them, they say "not good" if they want to be refined, and "not good" if they want to be vulgar. However, "not good" is not Suzhou dialect. If you use the soft language of Wu, there are various words of negation.

Suppose you bring up a person who is not welcome in Suzhou and deliberately ask the public:

Is so-and-so good?

Then! Suzhou people have various ways of expressing negation:

(1) So-and-so is "fu ling" (not effective/clever).

(2) So-and-so is "fu zhou" (not smooth/coordinated).

(3) So-and-so is "fu ru wei" (not flavorful/interesting).

(4) So-and-so is "fu ru diao" (not in tune/style).

These four kinds of negation all show that someone is not good; moreover, they are all very common words in Suzhou. You can say "fu ling," or you can say "fu zhou"; you can say "fu ru wei," or you can say "fu ru diao." If you study the origin of these various negations, saying "fu ling" is a negation from the witch doctor society; saying "fu zhou" is a negation from the machine weaving society; saying "fu ru wei" is a negation from the cook society; saying "fu ru diao" is a negation from the musician society. At first, these four kinds of sayings were all terms in each society, but later they became widespread, and everyone could say them to show that someone is not good.

However, when Wu people talk about a satisfactory person, they often say only one word "ling" or only one word "zhou," but they do not often say "ru wei" or "ru diao" alone. This is one difference. Moreover, "fu ling" and "fu zhou" can be said of all kinds of people; "fu ru wei" and "fu ru diao" are only applicable to criticize bad youths.

If an old man commits the faults of a bad youth, an "old" must be added to these two kinds of negations. Recently, an old painter in Wuzhong over sixty years old was sent to court for committing the crime of raping a young girl. In the places he passed through, Wu people often pointed at him like this:

Old "fu ru wei" Old "fu ru diao"

Record of the Shooting Sun Terrace

— Xu Siqiu

|Written in Opposition to Japan|

I have read the book Huainanzi. Hou Yi shot down the sun. It tells the story of the time of Emperor Yao, when ten suns appeared simultaneously, scorching the grass and trees. At that time, there was a king of the Youqiong State named Hou Yi, who was skilled in archery. Yao ordered him to shoot down the suns. He hit nine of them and left one. This is the origin of the "Shooting Sun."

Today, the violent suns are harming us, becoming more intense, even worse than the ancient ten suns appearing at the same time. Tens of thousands of square miles in the Northeast have been trampled all over. The blood of the Shanghai battle this spring has not yet dried, and recently, the news of alarm on the heated border has spread again. Although there are resistances from Ma Zhanshan, Ding Chao, Li Du, and various volunteer armies, their poisonous flames are fierce and have not been subdued. I hate that there is no Hou Yi reborn to shoot down the violent sun's arrogance and avenge our unprecedented disgrace!

My friend Chen Ziping is a patriot. His family is wealthy, and he is generous, repeatedly donating large sums of money to kill the enemy. Recently, he built a terrace in his garden called the "Shooting Sun Terrace." The terrace is square, about ten feet high, with a top that is round like a ball, painted bright red, resembling the shape of the sun. And with an arrow through its abdomen. Every morning, Chen brings a bow and arrows to the garden, stands dozens of paces away from the terrace, and shoots arrows at it, to show that he will not live under the same sky as the violent suns. This is why the terrace is named "Shooting Sun." Chen said: Although arrows are ancient weapons and are not suitable for today, once we serve on the battlefield, when engaging in close combat, striking first can inflict heavy damage on the enemy. This is another plan to shoot down the suns.

The day before yesterday, I accepted Chen's invitation to go and see it. In the garden, the golden wind was gentle, the leaves were falling, the autumn insects were chirping, as if mourning for the Northeast. The sun-shaped top of the terrace, battered by wind and rain, dripped with cold dew, and the abdomen was pierced by an arrow. After repeated shooting by Chen, the songs of Chu from all sides completely changed the old view. It is not precarious, is it about to collapse? Alas! I hope that our court and the people will be united in heart and mind, go to the great disaster together, wield Lu Yang's spear, hold Hou Yi's arrows, drive away these violent suns, and pacify the world. This is the essence of Chen's establishment of the Shooting Sun Terrace. Therefore, I write this record for it.

The Philosophy of Hats

— Lin

Some people say that marrying a wife is like buying a felt hat. The hats in the shop window, whether flat-brimmed or rolled-brimmed, whether gray or ochre, all seem beautiful and lovely; but once you buy one, you feel that the rolled-brimmed is better than the flat-brimmed; the gray one always seems not as good-looking as the ochre one, and the hat on your own head seems less beautiful than the one on someone else's head; but when you snatch someone else's hat and put it on your own head, you will immediately find some shortcomings and feel that your old hat is more suitable.

When choosing a hat, don't be too hasty, as haste will make you cheated; and don't be greedy for cheap, as greed will make you regret.

Buying a cheap hat will certainly not satisfy you; but wearing a hat that is too expensive will make you worry: you are afraid of it being blown away by the wind, and you are reluctant to let it get wet in the rain, it will hurt you if rats gnaw on it, and it will be enough to make you sad if a thief steals it; it is better to wear a cheap hat and be at ease, with a hundred and twenty percent peace of mind; you don't mind whether it is rainy or sunny, and even thieves don't bother to covet it.

The hat should not be too old-fashioned, so that people laugh at you; but it should not be too fashionable, so that people stare.

When buying a hat, it is better to buy it a little wider; if it is too tight, it will not be easy to take it on and off, and it will give you a headache when you wear it.

When someone "throws the top" off your head, don't shout for catching the thief or chase after them; because you can't get it back, and it's only funny to others, so what's the point? But you have to know that the reason why you were "thrown the top" is either because the hat is too beautiful, or because you were too careless and deliberately made the hat close to the streetcar window.

Taking a concubine is like buying a straw hat; a beautiful straw hat is really expensive, much more expensive than a felt hat, but it can only be shown off in the summer; when the autumn wind rises, you will think of the old felt hat thrown on top of the bed; take it out and have the laundry company wash it well, and then wear it on your head very comfortably; at that time, your straw hat may have been put on the head of a rickshaw puller as a rain hat, and you don't even want to think about it.

This is the life philosophy of hats!

Special Feature on the Vegetable Market

— Qian Taisheng

丨Oil, Salt, Soy Sauce, Vinegar, Vegetables, Rice, Firewood, 丨

Noise, disorder, shouting, arguing, dampness, fishiness, dirtiness, clamor—what can you feel in this special market? From the dim morning, when the sun barely penetrates the ground, fish, meat, chicken, duck, vegetables, and scallions are all busily laid out. Water is sprinkled on the ground, and a new day of trading begins.

The people who come to this market to buy food in large quantities are either chefs or stewards. Moreover, they come every day, very, very early, and are familiar with the fishmongers and butchers. Everything is relatively cheaper for them because they are their daily major customers, so it goes without saying that prices are lower. Then there are the maids from the mansions. They also come every day, but a step later than the stewards, and things are also much more expensive. By nine or ten o'clock, there are madams and mistresses who come by hired car with their fourteen-tael scales to the vegetable market. It's only natural that the vendors in the market use small scales, but since the mistresses and madams who come by hired car suspect the maids of pocketing money and fear the small scales in the market, they bring their own scales. But these, too, still measure fourteen taels.

Don't you see them arguing back and forth several times over a single copper coin's worth of business? Don't you see them grabbing an extra handful of bean sprouts after weighing ten copper coins' worth for the buyer? The vendors are certainly cunning, but they also have to make a living. The buyers want things to be cheap and plentiful. As a result, their lips get busy, and they argue until their saliva dries up. Besides these madams and mistresses, there are also the girls with disheveled hair, bare feet, and unbuttoned clothes. It's hard to imagine how they rushed here in such a hurry. And there are many who bring their beautiful clothes to the vegetable market as if they were going out. Perhaps they have forgotten that it is a dirty, smelly place.

This market with its peculiar smell and fishy odor also has many cooked food stalls where people can fill their stomachs. Noodles and beef soup are favorites for those who come to buy food in the morning.

The clamor gradually dissipates by noon. As the dim evening approaches, it becomes a "sleeping ground" that could not be better for the homeless!

Rotary Club Speech

Entering the Pass as Postal Comrades

— Seeking Happiness Studio Owner

(1)

Shenyang City superficially resembles a miniature model of Beiping City, in concrete and subtle detail. It is just as square, with nine city gates on all four sides, only the city walls are merely a fifth of the size of Beiping City, making it strangely exquisite!

Because the city's area is small, and its market has always been developed, it is difficult to cram all sorts of construction into that small city. The area of the four passes outside the city has been greatly expanded. The east, south, west, and north sides, about four or five li away from the city gate, have thus become industrial, commercial, and residential areas, collectively called the city passes, similar to the outer city of Beiping. Also, on the boundary of these city passes, along the thoroughfares leading to the nine city gates, various types of barrier gates have been built, called by names like such-and-such side gate or convenient gate.

The inner city has two gates on each of its four sides; although the format is common, the names distinguish between large and small. If there is a Large South Gate, there is also a Small South Gate; the same goes for the east and west sides; only the north side has a closed city gate between the Large North Gate and the Small North Gate, specifically built to complete the number of nine city gates, but it is not open. Therefore, there are only eight side gates. They are uniformly divided into Large East, Small East, Large West, Small West, Large South, Small South, Large North, Small North, evenly arranged on all four sides.

Especially the western side, going two or three li beyond the Large West and Small West side gates, there is the South Manchurian Railway Annex, occupied by the Japanese, with a circumference of twenty or thirty li, directly connecting to the South Manchurian Railway's "Fengtian" station, which they stubbornly insist on calling it. Due to the station, such a large annex was carved out, and people often collectively refer to it as the Japanese station or Japanese territory; all powers within are greater than those of concessions in other provinces, simply wanting to avoid acknowledging it as a concession and instead calling it an annex! It usually harbors dirt and accepts filth, doing everything possible, desperately trying to promote the prosperity of this annex, which consequently has combined the areas of Large West Pass, Small West Pass, Large West Side Gate, and Small West Side Gate outside Shenyang City into a very prosperous scene. But this prosperity cannot be picked up for nothing. Once they see it and become greedy, besides gradual encroachment, they can also sweep it all away in one go. Now, hasn't it all been thrown away for nothing? And what has been thrown away is not just these two West Passes, but the entire territory of Northeast China!

But tracing back to the source of the disaster, wasn't it that these two Large and Small West Passes were where they tentatively began their aggression? And on the evening of the September 18th Incident, the disaster also originated at the border of this annex, and the entire Shenyang City was easily obtained by the Japanese army, starting with the loss of the Large West and Small West city passes. A year has passed, but the national humiliation has not been avenged, and the lost territory has not been recovered. The September 18th anniversary has already been commemorated! Writing novels and coming to these most heartbreaking Large West and Small West two passes, I feel extremely painful and cannot help but waste a lot of blood and tears, writing in such a tedious manner; this is not something else, it is really because I cannot forget these two places in my heart!

Commercial News

Gold Price Rises Seven Taels Two Mace

Market Conditions Are Very Brisk. Yesterday, the gold market was exceptionally sharp and soaring, but there were no overly large fluctuations. The entire day only saw five taels of retracement, ultimately rising seven taels and some change. Initially, the spot silver market was quite stable, but the forward market plummeted. American cotton futures also fell by more than forty pounds. In particular, news reported that Mexico was aggressively purchasing cash to prepare for switching to the gold standard. With these several major reasons, the market opened high, nearing the 740 tael mark. However, major players, considering the excessive rise and the opportune moment, tended to sell. Moreover, as foreign exchange turned from firm to loose, banks were strongly inclined to sell, so the trend softened, sharply falling by three or four taels. However, there was only a return of one or two taels at midday, and the afternoon market was uneventful. The selling pressure continued, and the situation seemed weak. However, near the close, it became slightly more peaceful, as the price remained above 735 taels, and traders' confidence was very strong. All October contracts, around 300 lots, were traded by Tongfeng Heng, Ruixing Yuanmao Yong, Dacheng, etc., discounted by three to two and a half mace. Due to price disagreements, the spot market did not see any transactions. Now, the detailed history of the past market conditions, both before and after, is listed below.

Early Opening Jumps Wildly by Eleven Taels. The November contract opened at 739.5 taels, a sharp increase of eleven taels (before the market opened, it had reached forty taels in the goods market). Yuhe Yuanchun and others immediately purchased at the listed price, so market conditions were particularly firm. As for large bars, they only rose by one-sixteenth. The silver price did not change, but private telegraphs reported an increase of five-sixteenths. Furthermore, the spot silver futures at the Gold Exchange suddenly rebounded by more than three li, leading to highly elevated sentiment. Subsequently, as Tongtaichang Heng, Yu Fuchang, Yongfeng Yuantai, Yuanmao Yong, and Dalian merchants took advantage of this to sell, it immediately dropped by more than one tael, to 37.8 mace. At this time, HSBC and others offered December US dollars at 375, November at 25. In an instant, Yuanchun, Yuankangxiang, Bingxing Qian, Changxiang Dadecheng, Yifeng Yongfu Yu, etc., bought in, and it rose again by one tael, to 39 taels.
